<meta name="description" content="Tracking threat actors in the long run is a fundamental part of the cyber threat intelligence program we run at Yoroi, few years ago we began monitoring a particular actor who started offensive operations even in the Italian landscape: Aggah (TH-157), who launched malicious campaign such as the Roma225 and the RG ones against the Italian manufacturing vertical. At that time, even UNIT42 was closely monitoring that actor, unveiling a large scale operation threatening also United States, Europe and Asia."/>

		<main id="swup" class="ct-div-block " ><div id="div_block-1-4186" class="ct-div-block bg-dark" ><img  id="image-2-4186" alt="Yoroi Background" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/Risorsa-36-8.png" class="ct-image bg-heading"/><section id="section-3-4186" class=" ct-section section intro" ><div class="ct-section-inner-wrap"><h1 id="headline-4-4186" class="ct-headline intro__heading"><span id="span-5-4186" class="ct-span" >The "WayBack” Campaign: a Large Scale Operation Hiding in Plain Sight</span></h1><div id="code_block-28-4186" class="ct-code-block" ><h6 class="blog-post-date">
	06/29/2021</h6></div><div id="text_block-14-4186" class="ct-text-block blog-post" ><span id="span-15-4186" class="ct-span oxy-stock-content-styles blog-post" >
<h1 class="wp-block-heading">Introduction&nbsp;</h1>



<p>Tracking threat actors&nbsp;in the long run&nbsp;is a fundamental&nbsp;part of the cyber threat intelligence program we run at&nbsp;Yoroi,&nbsp;few years ago&nbsp;we began&nbsp;monitoring&nbsp;a particular actor who started offensive operations even in the Italian landscape:&nbsp;Aggah&nbsp;(TH-157), who launched malicious campaign such as&nbsp;the&nbsp;&nbsp;<a href="https://yoroi.company/research/the-enigmatic-roma225-campaign/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Roma225</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;the&nbsp;<a href="https://yoroi.company/research/the-evolution-of-aggah-from-roma225-to-the-rg-campaign/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">RG</a>&nbsp;ones&nbsp;against&nbsp;the&nbsp;Italian manufacturing&nbsp;vertical. At that time, even&nbsp;UNIT42 was&nbsp;closely&nbsp;monitoring&nbsp;that&nbsp;actor, unveiling a&nbsp;<a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/aggah-campaign-bit-ly-blogspot-and-pastebin-used-for-c2-in-large-scale-campaign/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">large scale operation</a>&nbsp;threatening&nbsp;also&nbsp;United States,&nbsp;Europe&nbsp;and Asia.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The&nbsp;recent&nbsp;operation we tracked was designed to delivery over 900 pieces of malware with highly dangerous&nbsp;capabilities&nbsp;enabling the threat actor&nbsp;to conduct both digital and environmental monitoring&nbsp;of their victims across the globe.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The attribution&nbsp;of this operations&nbsp;is&nbsp;far from certainty&nbsp;and&nbsp;such activities&nbsp;could&nbsp;be&nbsp;possibly&nbsp;related&nbsp;to the threat group&nbsp;named&nbsp;Gorgon/Subaat.&nbsp;Anyway,&nbsp;based on the modus operandi,&nbsp;with no doubt&nbsp;this&nbsp;actor&nbsp;is&nbsp;heavily active&nbsp;at least&nbsp;since&nbsp;2019&nbsp;and equally certain it is insisting&nbsp;in&nbsp;the&nbsp;European and Italian landscape, so the&nbsp;Yoroi&nbsp;Malware ZLAB is monitoring&nbsp;the evolution of its TTPs to ensure proactive defense to&nbsp;Yoroi&nbsp;customers&nbsp;and recently we intercepted a new offensive operation&nbsp;leveraging&nbsp;new&nbsp;<a href="https://yoroi.company/research/aggah-how-to-run-a-botnet-without-renting-a-server-for-more-than-a-year/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">serverless</a>&nbsp;techniques to bypass traditional security&nbsp;defenses to&nbsp;target&nbsp;many&nbsp;European and Italian organizations: we named it the “WayBack&nbsp;campaign”.&nbsp;</p>



<h1 class="wp-block-heading">The&nbsp;“WayBack”&nbsp;Campaign&nbsp;</h1>



<p>During our investigation we noticed&nbsp;the attack&nbsp;we were looking at,&nbsp;was just a piece of a wider offensive campaign lasting for months. In fact, the analysis of the infection chain&nbsp;revealed the actor has&nbsp;established&nbsp;the new TTPs&nbsp;at least&nbsp;since April 2021, and many other attach&nbsp;waves&nbsp;were prepared and launched during that time.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Based on the evidence found during the attacker infrastructure analysis we reconstructed&nbsp;at least&nbsp;six&nbsp;offensive waves part of this campaign:&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list"><li>April 24&nbsp;</li><li>May 12&nbsp;</li><li>May 19&nbsp;</li><li>May 26-28&nbsp;</li><li>June 1-3&nbsp;</li><li>June&nbsp;7-10&nbsp;</li></ul>



<p>We&nbsp;observed&nbsp;an evolution on the techniques of this&nbsp;threat actor, but his strategic choice&nbsp;remains&nbsp;constant in time: a large amount of the malware delivery infrastructure is still serverless.&nbsp;In the last three months&nbsp;Aggah, potentially linked with the&nbsp;APT&nbsp;group&nbsp;<a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/unit42-gorgon-group-slithering-nation-state-cybercrime/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Gorgon/Subaat</a>,&nbsp;leveraged&nbsp;other&nbsp;different&nbsp;legit third-party services&nbsp;in a multi-stage fashion&nbsp;(T1608)&nbsp;to bypass security control&nbsp;and&nbsp;gain the&nbsp;initial&nbsp;foothold into&nbsp;the target organizations. Traditionally,&nbsp;the&nbsp;actor&nbsp;was heavily abusing&nbsp;Pastebin&nbsp;services to host and drop malicious code, but in the latest campaign they abuse Internet Archive, the popular&nbsp;nonprofit&nbsp;service created to help the internet community to store pass on the&nbsp;today's&nbsp;open&nbsp;knowledge to our heirs.&nbsp;</p>



<p>In fact, the actor hosted a huge volume of malicious code inside the “Community Texts” repositories of the Internet Archive project&nbsp;using multiple accounts on the platform, masking their&nbsp;malicious&nbsp;tool as&nbsp;open books and texts.&nbsp;More details on the accounts&nbsp;leveraged&nbsp;by the threat actor (T1583.006) on section “Abused Accounts in the “Wayback” campaign”.&nbsp;</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">The “Wayback”&nbsp;Campaign&nbsp;Infection&nbsp;Chain&nbsp;&nbsp;</h2>



<p>To get an&nbsp;immediate&nbsp;outlook of the mechanisms behind the “WayBack” campaign, we prepared an&nbsp;infographic comprehensive of all the capabilities and the extension, in terms of both serverless mechanisms and deployed payloads, of all the entire malicious infrastructure.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="309" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-1-1024x309.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5186" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-1-1024x309.png 1024w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-1-300x91.png 300w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-1-768x232.png 768w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-1.png 1332w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 1: The “Wayback” Campaign attack chain&nbsp;</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Abused Accounts in the “WayBack”&nbsp;campaign&nbsp;</h2>



<p>A necessary deepening point is the malware delivery infrastructure of the “WayBack” campaign. During our inspections we&nbsp;observed&nbsp;that the actor&nbsp;mainly&nbsp;operated&nbsp;through three accounts on the Internet Archive repository.&nbsp;</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list"><li>https:// archive .org/details/@muhammad_tauseef_aslam</li><li>https:// archive .org/details/@kut404</li><li>https:// archive .org/details/@Gpt </li></ul>



<p>These accounts have been abused by the threat actors at least since April 2021.&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter"><img decoding="async" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-1024x473.png" alt="This image has an empty alt attribute; its file name is image-1024x473.png"/></figure></div>

<p>Putting the principal malware delivery infrastructure deployment activities in a timeline helps understanding how intense the whole malicious operation has been, in fact the actor was especially active around 1st, 8th and 9th June with peaks in the weaponization phase (TA0042).&nbsp;</p>

<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Actor Flashcard&nbsp;</h2>



<p>To summarize how this actor is&nbsp;operating&nbsp;we prepared a synthetic&nbsp;flashcard capturing the main techniques&nbsp;observed&nbsp;during the campaign operation.&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="998" height="725" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-7.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5193" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-7.png 998w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-7-300x218.png 300w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-7-768x558.png 768w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 998px) 100vw, 998px" /><figcaption>Figure 3. Actor flashcard</figcaption></figure></div>



<h1 class="wp-block-heading">Technical Analysis&nbsp;</h1>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table><tbody><tr><td><strong>Hash</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>df91f20f8204e6d0e1239202c58d438143ccc560ac5ae8b2d8cf8e49aaae370&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Threat</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>Aggah&nbsp;campaign May 2021&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Brief Description</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>Malicious PPA macro&nbsp;dropper&nbsp;&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Ssdeep</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>192:ZMABVcV5JnWrKPfvEdkGsJ9s4cTERRA+o3Mz:PVOWrKPIsrsDEocz&nbsp;</td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Table 1: Static information about the sample&nbsp;</p>



<p>The infection starts&nbsp;with&nbsp;a malicious&nbsp;Powerpoint&nbsp;file weaponized with a&nbsp;malicious macro, as&nbsp;a&nbsp;major part of the multi-stage chains. The macro in this case is easy to decode and&nbsp;it is&nbsp;the following:&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="642" height="624" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-4.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5190" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-4.png 642w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-4-300x292.png 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 642px) 100vw, 642px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 4:&nbsp;&nbsp;Malicious Macro evidence&nbsp;</p>



<p>One thing to notice&nbsp;here is the&nbsp;assignment&nbsp;GetObject("new:F935DC22-1CF0-11D0-ADB9-00C04FD58A0B"): it is the&nbsp;<a href="https://www.fireeye.com/blog/threat-research/2019/06/hunting-com-objects.html" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">CLSID key</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;WindowsScriptHost&nbsp;COM Object. COM objects have been an interesting area for Security Researchers for some time, especially&nbsp;its usage in&nbsp;penetration testing. Additionally,&nbsp;the&nbsp;<a href="https://evilcodeanalysis.com/2021/03/01/asyncrat-delivery-technique-10-minute-analysis/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">MSHTA</a>&nbsp;is a common LOLBIN to execute remote files&nbsp;the actor abuses from long time.&nbsp;</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Dynamic&nbsp;Malware&nbsp;Infrastructure Generation&nbsp;</h2>



<p>During&nbsp;the static inspection of the&nbsp;compiled&nbsp;VBA&nbsp;macro project&nbsp;named “titu.bin”,&nbsp;we noticed that&nbsp;that above mentioned&nbsp;bitly&nbsp;link&nbsp;is not&nbsp;the only one: in fact,&nbsp;there&nbsp;are&nbsp;many&nbsp;bitly&nbsp;links hidden&nbsp;inside:&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="639" height="518" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-8.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5194" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-8.png 639w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-8-300x243.png 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 639px) 100vw, 639px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 5:&nbsp; Piece of the list of&nbsp;bitly&nbsp;pages&nbsp;</p>



<p>All of them&nbsp;are&nbsp;functional and point to a different blogger&nbsp;page.&nbsp;This&nbsp;mechanism&nbsp;is used&nbsp;to&nbsp;update the&nbsp;distribution infrastructure by&nbsp;only changing the&nbsp;redirection URLs.&nbsp;At the time of writing some of them are offline, but most of them are still redirecting to the&nbsp;second layer of the malware distribution infrastructure.&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="337" height="457" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-3.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5189" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-3.png 337w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-3-221x300.png 221w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 337px) 100vw, 337px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 6:&nbsp; List of the&nbsp;blogspot&nbsp;pages&nbsp;</p>



<p>The&nbsp;bitly&nbsp;urls&nbsp;land&nbsp;on&nbsp;the&nbsp;several&nbsp;blogspot&nbsp;pages. Each of these HTML pages&nbsp;contain&nbsp;an&nbsp;obfuscated&nbsp;Windows Script Host&nbsp;JavaScript&nbsp;code&nbsp;mimicking common&nbsp;javascript&nbsp;codes we can find in every&nbsp;web pages.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<pre class="wp-block-code"><code>&lt;script language=javascript&gt;document.write(unescape( 
'URL-ESCAPE ENCODED PAYLOAD' 
))&lt;/script&gt; </code></pre>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Code&nbsp;Snippet&nbsp;1: Pseudocode executed by the MSHTA Engine&nbsp;</p>



<p>We identifier all&nbsp;the codes hidden in the blogpost pages and through them, we were able to retrieve another large series of&nbsp;dropurls&nbsp;pointing to another layer of the distribution infrastructure. We found not&nbsp;only&nbsp;addresses belonging to the classis Blogspot pages, but also belonging to&nbsp;Web Archive, the famous platform to conserve the&nbsp;historical internet pages.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Landing into the&nbsp;Internet&nbsp;Archive&nbsp;</h2>



<p>Analyzing the hidden JavaScript code in the blogger pages&nbsp;we&nbsp;recognized the&nbsp;classic&nbsp;obfuscation&nbsp;pattern&nbsp;we saw in&nbsp;past&nbsp;Aggah&nbsp;campaigns:&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="487" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-22-1024x487.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5209" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-22-1024x487.png 1024w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-22-300x143.png 300w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-22-768x365.png 768w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-22.png 1217w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 7:&nbsp; Example of MSHTA code&nbsp;</p>



<p>After&nbsp;the&nbsp;decoding,&nbsp;we have&nbsp;a&nbsp;cleaner view of the&nbsp;malicious code executed though the MSHTA engine:&nbsp;Aggah&nbsp;downloads many pieces&nbsp;of&nbsp;powershell&nbsp;code from archive.org, the official Internet Archive project domain.&nbsp;</p>

<p class="has-text-align-center">Code&nbsp;Snippet&nbsp;2: Decoded script&nbsp;</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">The&nbsp;Payload&nbsp;Delivery&nbsp;</h2>



<p>We focused&nbsp;on the Invoke-Expression cmdlet which downloads and execute from&nbsp;the&nbsp;Web Archive Page. The structure of the&nbsp;Powershell&nbsp;script looks like the following:&nbsp;</p>



<pre class="wp-block-code"><code>[String]$InterserverLogin='PAYLOAD TO INJECT IN HEX FORMAT' 
Function FHGJKLHJKGJFHJGKJHLIHKVJGCJVHBKJ { 
  
    [CmdletBinding()] 
    [OutputType([byte[]])] 
    param( 
        [Parameter(Mandatory=$true)] [String]$H3 
    ) 
    $vbdhjujusyujczz = New-Object -TypeName byte[] -ArgumentList ($H3.Length / 2) 
    for ($i = 0; $i -lt $H3.Length; $i += 2) { 
        $vbdhjujusyujczz[$i / 2] = [Convert]::ToByte($H3.Substring($i, 2), 16) 
    } 
  
    return [byte[]]$vbdhjujusyujczz 
} 
  
  
[String]$yrryyuxvsdsf='PROCESS HOLLOWIG MODULE' 
[Byte[]]$H5=FHGJKLHJKGJFHJGKJHLIHKVJGCJVHBKJ $yrryyuxvsdsf 
[Byte[]]$H6= FHGJKLHJKGJFHJGKJHLIHKVJGCJVHBKJ $InterserverLogin 
[Byte[]]$H5=FHGJKLHJKGJFHJGKJHLIHKVJGCJVHBKJ $yrryyuxvsdsf 
$ali = "C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework\v4.0.30319\MSBuild.exe" 
[Reflection.Assembly]::Load($H5).GetType('WpfControlLibrary1.LOGO').GetMethod('bit_alosh').Invoke($null,[object[]] ($ali,$H6))</code></pre>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Code&nbsp;Snippet&nbsp;3: Payload on the Web Archive page&nbsp;</p>



<p>Also,&nbsp;this structure remarks the classic TTPs&nbsp;observed&nbsp;during&nbsp;the&nbsp;previous&nbsp;campaign. We have a module for the Process Hollowing technique to inject the&nbsp;final payload inside the designed process. In this case is MSBuild.exe a basic executable of the .NET environment.&nbsp;</p>



<p>&nbsp;<br>This malicious routine is performed through the last line of the PowerShell code:&nbsp;</p>



<pre class="wp-block-code"><code>“[Reflection.Assembly]::Load($H5).GetType('WpfControlLibrary1.LOGO').GetMethod('bit_alosh').Invoke($null,[object[]] ($ali,$H6))” </code></pre>



<p></p>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Code Snippet 4: .NET Assembly loading in PowerShell evidence&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="430" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-10-1024x430.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5196" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-10-1024x430.png 1024w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-10-300x126.png 300w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-10-768x322.png 768w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-10.png 1211w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 8: Process hollowing&nbsp;malicious&nbsp;DLL&nbsp;evidence&nbsp;</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Dissecting the Payloads&nbsp;</h2>



<p>As we discussed inside the "The&nbsp;Wayback&nbsp;Campaign" section, we&nbsp;observed&nbsp;the threat actor deployed many different payloads on the platform and in most cases, they are each other different, for this reason we decided to&nbsp;explore those malware and study them&nbsp;in order to&nbsp;identify&nbsp;what type of threats it has decided to carry out in its malicious campaigns.&nbsp;Many of them were commodity malware customized by the actor.&nbsp;</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading">Agent Tesla&nbsp;</h3>



<p>The&nbsp;first sample is the one retrieved from the <a href="https://ia601409.us.archive[.]org/4/items/Re-Panel-24/10.txt" rel="nofollow">https://ia601409.us.archive[.]org/4/items/Re-Panel-24/10.txt</a> and after a quick triaging operation, we categorized the sample as Agent Tesla&nbsp;info&nbsp;stealer.&nbsp;</p>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table><tbody><tr><td><strong>Hash</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>8165b1162eb2b4ba988fa313a4c612473b3c8dd20be7d27b6ee81435ed984a7c&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Threat</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>Aggah&nbsp;campaign May 2021&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Brief Description</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>Agent Tesla Payload&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Ssdeep</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>3072:F+Ew5uDJoIefh/46uKWqu6xHfnIAU/FF75+VD31I/8dzflROzu5F2xr+hxmleYNe:Mn46uKWqu6xVULklI/8xlX5AAhxaNU&nbsp;</td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Table&nbsp;2: Static information about the sample&nbsp;</p>



<p>The malware&nbsp;does not&nbsp;seems&nbsp;to have&nbsp;an elevated level&nbsp;of&nbsp;obfuscation&nbsp;and it starts with&nbsp;a check of a security privileges, aimed to be an&nbsp;elementary evasion technique because the older machines&nbsp;don’t&nbsp;implement&nbsp;the modern SSL and TLS newest versions.&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="297" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-9-1024x297.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5195" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-9-1024x297.png 1024w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-9-300x87.png 300w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-9-768x223.png 768w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-9.png 1139w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 9: Check of security protocols&nbsp;</p>



<p>After that check, the malware&nbsp;behaves like the classic&nbsp;AgentTesla&nbsp;malware family and continues with&nbsp;its own info stealing operations, retrieving all the&nbsp;sensitive data&nbsp;about the victim machine, browser cache and cookies, Mail&nbsp;clients'&nbsp;credentials, Crypto wallets,&nbsp;Clipboard data etc.&nbsp;It sends all of it to its&nbsp;C2.&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="633" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-13-1024x633.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5199" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-13-1024x633.png 1024w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-13-300x185.png 300w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-13-768x475.png 768w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-13.png 1086w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 10: C2 communication evidence&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading">Agent Tesla&nbsp;FTP&nbsp;</h3>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table><tbody><tr><td><strong>Hash</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>5b8643a221d028761328525ec881250fb02840f97792557020a49a226d23e7e6&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Threat</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>Aggah&nbsp;campaign May 2021&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Brief Description</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>Agent Tesla Payload&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Ssdeep</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>6144:1ey6uKWqu6ac5UkxBM/n3w07dXaTd66VU:1eJ3xW/HdXaTt&nbsp;</td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Table 3:&nbsp; Static Information about the sample&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<p>Even&nbsp;this second&nbsp;wave of malware&nbsp;contains&nbsp;a series of Agent Tesla samples, but they&nbsp;have got&nbsp;a different configuration. The sample performs the same info stealing operations, so we&nbsp;concentrated on the C2 extraction,&nbsp;and this time it is an&nbsp;FTP C2 pointing to another&nbsp;IP. The C2 config is the following.&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="687" height="55" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-6.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5192" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-6.png 687w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-6-300x24.png 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 687px) 100vw, 687px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 11: C2 FTP protocol evidence&nbsp;</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading">Oski&nbsp;Stealer&nbsp;</h3>



<p>In this campaign the threat actor changed final payload to deliver, now we have&nbsp;found&nbsp;Oski&nbsp;stealer.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table><tbody><tr><td><strong>Hash</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>fcc311967558ab8b02cbda8a6a30b3f2bcb606542da4f7aeb23648daa985035a&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Threat</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>Aggah&nbsp;campaign&nbsp;June&nbsp;2021&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Brief Description</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>Oski&nbsp;stealer&nbsp;Payload&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Ssdeep</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>6144:WfUauY68uSWCx+XA7mg2pNG1Ljo3cZEHc39:WwY68u1Cx+wm/pCsv&nbsp;</td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Table 4: Static information about the sample&nbsp;</p>



<p>The sample is compilated in C++ and it&nbsp;does not&nbsp;show any&nbsp;evidence&nbsp;of&nbsp;obfuscation.&nbsp;Moreover,&nbsp;we also noticed the&nbsp;classic string-decoding routine of this malware family.&nbsp;It stores a long series of configuration strings in a base base64 format and encrypted with the RC4&nbsp;algorithm, like the following way:&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="928" height="442" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-15.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5201" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-15.png 928w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-15-300x143.png 300w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-15-768x366.png 768w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 928px) 100vw, 928px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure&nbsp;12:&nbsp;Evidence of decoding routine&nbsp;</p>



<p>So,&nbsp;we decoded them&nbsp;and&nbsp;reported&nbsp;the configurations strings&nbsp;in the Appendix “Oski/Vidar Configuration&nbsp;strings”.&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="256" height="37" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-5.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5191"/></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure&nbsp;13: Evidence of the C2&nbsp;configuration&nbsp;</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading">The&nbsp;Cobian&nbsp;RAT&nbsp;</h3>



<p>During the study of the campaigns, we focused on another peculiar sample, way less common than the&nbsp;previous&nbsp;ones.&nbsp;It is written in .NET&nbsp;framework,&nbsp;and we decided to investigate it.&nbsp;</p>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table><tbody><tr><td><strong>Hash</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>152b770f144ba5c60f8d0958f5eb2a8844e88ae3dc847c1e6c5ee9df96a62f83&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Threat</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>Aggah&nbsp;campaign June 2021&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Brief Description</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>Cobian&nbsp;Payload&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Ssdeep</strong>&nbsp;</td><td>1536:pXsqEjnYi9bkY6yhLoYtVc9591ocOzUD:pcvbYi9bkEHc39FOI&nbsp;</td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Table 5: Static information about the sample&nbsp;</p>



<p>The sample is packed with the famous .NET Reactor&nbsp;packer,&nbsp;so&nbsp;it is easy to unpack:&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="369" height="218" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-14.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5200" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-14.png 369w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-14-300x177.png 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 369px) 100vw, 369px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 14: Packer Evidence&nbsp;</p>



<p>After that, we&nbsp;proceeded&nbsp;to study the malicious code&nbsp;to&nbsp;understand the malware capabilities.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="604" height="219" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-12.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5198" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-12.png 604w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-12-300x109.png 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 604px) 100vw, 604px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 15: Evidence of the classic Cobian malware behavior&nbsp;</p>



<p>By statically&nbsp;analyzing&nbsp;the code, two interesting&nbsp;strings&nbsp;emerge,&nbsp;the&nbsp;classic “HKCU/Software/Microsoft/CurrentVersion/Run”&nbsp;registry key aimed at setting the persistence, and a&nbsp;malformed&nbsp;IP, because the last octet is more than 255. But debugging, the&nbsp;mystery&nbsp;is resolved: the code reverts the string and the actual IP C2 is 193[.56.29.171:&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="731" height="619" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-16.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5202" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-16.png 731w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-16-300x254.png 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 731px) 100vw, 731px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 16: String Reverse evidence to restore the actual&nbsp;C2&nbsp;</p>



<p>After preparing the C2's IP to connect, the malware&nbsp;initiates&nbsp;a Socket to it and waits for the receipt of the commands, unfortunately, during the analysis the server was&nbsp;unresponsive,&nbsp;and we weren't able to recover the command list.&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="776" height="534" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-21.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5208" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-21.png 776w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-21-300x206.png 300w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-21-768x528.png 768w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 776px) 100vw, 776px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 17: C2 communication routine evidence&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<p>This malware is a Cobian RAT v2.0 sample and&nbsp;by statically inspecting the code, we carried out all the most important command instructed to be executed by that rudimentary backdoor:&nbsp;</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list"><li>Execute commands coming from the&nbsp;C2&nbsp;</li><li>List all the active windows&nbsp;&nbsp;</li><li>Record the&nbsp;camera&nbsp;</li><li>Get Information about the HDD&nbsp;</li><li>Take&nbsp;screenshots&nbsp;</li><li>Gather sensitive data to send to&nbsp;C2&nbsp;</li><li>Modify file&nbsp;permissions&nbsp;</li><li>Modify the&nbsp;firewall&nbsp;permissions&nbsp;</li></ul>



<p>Earlier Cobian RAT&nbsp;versions were analyzed&nbsp;by&nbsp;<a href="https://www.zscaler.com/blogs/security-research/cobian-rat-backdoored-rat" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">ZScaler</a>&nbsp;security researchers back in 2017. In their report they documented&nbsp;an interesting&nbsp;fact: that&nbsp;old&nbsp;Cobian RAT sample they investigated was&nbsp;backdoored to retrieve&nbsp;commands from certain&nbsp;Pastebin&nbsp;pages.&nbsp;</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading">The&nbsp;Persistence components&nbsp;</h3>



<p>After&nbsp;providing&nbsp;an&nbsp;overview&nbsp;of all the malicious payload delivered by all the campaigns, we go back to&nbsp;the inspection of the code seen in "Code Snippet&nbsp;2"&nbsp;to&nbsp;identify&nbsp;the&nbsp;persistence&nbsp;mechanisms adopted by the threat actor.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<p>It&nbsp;is quite noisy because it creates&nbsp;four&nbsp;keys&nbsp;inside the classic&nbsp;path, as shown in the following figure:&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="106" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-11-1024x106.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5197" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-11-1024x106.png 1024w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-11-300x31.png 300w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-11-768x79.png 768w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-11.png 1154w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 18: Evidence of the set registry&nbsp;keys&nbsp;</p>



<p>Not only, it creates also a scheduled task repeating every 80 minutes:&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="640" height="182" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-19.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5205" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-19.png 640w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-19-300x85.png 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 19: Evidence of the scheduled task&nbsp;</p>



<p>Those persistence mechanisms are designed to give the actor&nbsp;an important level&nbsp;of resilience&nbsp;and modularity&nbsp;of the entire infrastructure.&nbsp;However, a simple antimalware engine&nbsp;could be&nbsp;able to detect all of them.&nbsp;Besides this consideration,&nbsp;let's&nbsp;analyze all the five&nbsp;persistence components:&nbsp;</p>



<ol class="wp-block-list"><li>“Backpup” registry key:&nbsp;this registry key points to the&nbsp;“hxxps://<strong>papagujjiiiiii</strong>[.]blogspot[.]com/p/10.html”&nbsp;blogspot&nbsp;page which, during our investigation was&nbsp;unregistered.&nbsp;</li></ol>



<ol class="wp-block-list" start="2"><li>"care” registry key:&nbsp;this second registry key points to&nbsp;powershell&nbsp;code which&nbsp;unleashes the download of the&nbsp;paylaods&nbsp;described in the&nbsp;previous&nbsp;section.&nbsp;</li></ol>



<ol class="wp-block-list" start="3"><li>"task1” registry key:&nbsp;this&nbsp;registry key points to&nbsp;"hxxps://<strong>9ke6n</strong>.blogspot[.]com/p/10.html"&nbsp;blogspot&nbsp;page which&nbsp;downloads a&nbsp;complex&nbsp;powershell&nbsp;script aimed at putting to zero the protection systems of the victim machine. It&nbsp;downloads&nbsp;a&nbsp;powershell&nbsp;script from a “usrfiles” platform, a sort&nbsp;of file sharing platform.&nbsp;&nbsp;</li></ol>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1024" height="145" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-17-1024x145.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5203" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-17-1024x145.png 1024w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-17-300x42.png 300w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-17-768x108.png 768w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-17.png 1515w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 20: Evidence of the main script on&nbsp;usrfiles&nbsp;platform&nbsp;</p>



<p>As shown in the figure, it downloads other three components from the same platform:&nbsp;</p>



<p>1)&nbsp;The first one is the actual malicious script which&nbsp;disables&nbsp;every type of security&nbsp;protection, such as Windows Defender, UAC controls, Firewall, whitelisting some processes&nbsp;(obvious&nbsp;mshta,&nbsp;powershell,&nbsp;cmd, explorer,&nbsp;MsBuild&nbsp;etc), Microsoft Office.&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="972" height="975" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-20.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5206" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-20.png 972w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-20-300x300.png 300w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-20-150x150.png?crop=1 150w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-20-768x770.png 768w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 972px) 100vw, 972px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 21: Piece of the malicious script aimed at putting to zero the security of the victim&nbsp;machine&nbsp;</p>



<p>2)&nbsp;In&nbsp;order&nbsp;to&nbsp;work, it needs to have the administration privileges which are granted by the usage of the so-called "fodhelper&nbsp;UAC bypass", a&nbsp;well-known&nbsp;documented technique&nbsp;in red-team activities and we&nbsp;encountered&nbsp;in&nbsp;a previous&nbsp;attack chain of the same actor. This technique is guaranteed by the second file on the "usrfiles" platform:&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="972" height="975" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-20.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5207" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-20.png 972w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-20-300x300.png 300w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-20-150x150.png?crop=1 150w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-20-768x770.png 768w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 972px) 100vw, 972px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 22:&nbsp;FodHelper&nbsp;UAC bypass technique evidence&nbsp;</p>



<p>3)&nbsp;The last file is the&nbsp;simplest, it&nbsp;has to&nbsp;start all the security&nbsp;destruction&nbsp;process:&nbsp;</p>



<div class="wp-block-image"><figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="886" height="90" src="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-18.png" alt="" class="wp-image-5204" srcset="https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-18.png 886w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-18-300x30.png 300w, https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/image-18-768x78.png 768w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 886px) 100vw, 886px" /></figure></div>



<p class="has-text-align-center">Figure 23: Starting routine&nbsp;evidence&nbsp;</p>



<p>As shown in the first script, all these components will be stored into the folder "C:\Users\Public\" as&nbsp;VBS&nbsp;scripts.&nbsp;</p>



<p>1)&nbsp;"task2” registry key:&nbsp;During our analysis, the&nbsp;URL&nbsp;pointed by the task has been registered by the actor, but there&nbsp;wasn't&nbsp;any malicious script to execute.&nbsp;Probably the&nbsp;actor&nbsp;will use that&nbsp;URL&nbsp;as backup or in a second moment.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<p>2)&nbsp;"SECOTAKSA"&nbsp;scheduled task:&nbsp;This task points to&nbsp;"hxxps://<strong>0v2x</strong>.blogspot[.]com/p/10.html" which&nbsp;downloads&nbsp;the last version of the payload from one of the mentioned Web Archive folders.&nbsp;</p>



<h1 class="wp-block-heading">Conclusion&nbsp;</h1>



<p>The malicious campaign we tracked has delivered over 450 distinct&nbsp;malwares&nbsp;to multiple targets all around the world. Most of the malicious code distributed by the&nbsp;Aggah&nbsp;actor&nbsp;is able to&nbsp;seriously&nbsp;violate the confidentiality of digital&nbsp;and voice&nbsp;communications&nbsp;of targeted users due to the impactful nature of the capabilities of the malicious tools: almost all of them&nbsp;can&nbsp;get full remote control&nbsp;and hands on keyboard access&nbsp;to&nbsp;targeted endpoints, some of them are also able to intercept environmental&nbsp;conversations&nbsp;and silently collect video streams directly from the laptop webcam.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Like in past operations, this enigmatic&nbsp;actor is still&nbsp;leveraging&nbsp;commodity malware to conduct large scale espionage operations, manipulating it to bypass security controls and antiviruses.&nbsp;We also noticed an evolution in the delivery infrastructure related to the abuse of Internet Archive service, a&nbsp;well-known,&nbsp;high reputation,&nbsp;service. Despite this tactical change, many pillars of its delivery operations&nbsp;remain&nbsp;stable such as the usage of PowerPoint presentations,&nbsp;shortening services and script hiding techniques on legit blogging platforms.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Multi-modular and multi-stage attack chain grant attackers’&nbsp;high level&nbsp;of resilience and self-customization of the&nbsp;payloads and&nbsp;makes traditional detection and blocking less effective.&nbsp;Yoroi&nbsp;protects its customers from this kind of threat&nbsp;leveraging&nbsp;the Yomi sandbox technologies,&nbsp;Genku&nbsp;network probes and&nbsp;Kanwa endpoint agent, along with precise, human refined Threat Intelligence to&nbsp;protect&nbsp;and respond&nbsp;to&nbsp;modern&nbsp;cyber&nbsp;threats.&nbsp;</p>

<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Yara Rules&nbsp;</h2>



<pre class="wp-block-code"><code>rule CobianRAT { 
meta: 
  	description = "Yara Rule for Cobian RAT in Aggah Wayback campaign" 
  	author = "Yoroi Malware Zlab" 
  	last_updated = "2021_06_18" 
  	tlp = "white" 
  	category = "informational" 

strings: 
$s1="bWFzdGVy" wide
$s2="Ydmzipw~" wide 

$a1={11 8E B7 16 FE 01 5F 2C 46 1B 8D 1D} 
$a2={07 17 D6 0B 07 1A 30 20 14 0C 07 B5 1F 64 28 33} 

condition: 
   uint16(0) == 0x5A4D and any of ($s*) and 1 of ($a*)
} </code></pre>

function checkElement() {
    var targetElements = document.querySelectorAll('.wpcf7-response-output[aria-hidden="true"]');
    targetElements.forEach(function(element) {
		const regex = /Thank you for your message\. It has been sent\.|There was an error trying to send your message\. Please try again later\./
        if (regex.test(element.textContent.trim())) {
            console.log('Target element detected:', element.textContent);
            location.href = 'https://yoroi.company/wp-content/uploads/2024/04/2024_Yoroi_Cybersecurity_Annual_Report.pdf'
        }
    });
}

var interval = setInterval(checkElement, 3000);
</script>

		         <path d="M16 7.781c-4.537 0-8.219 3.681-8.219 8.219s3.681 8.219 8.219 8.219 8.219-3.681 8.219-8.219c0-4.537-3.681-8.219-8.219-8.219zM16 21.331c-2.944 0-5.331-2.387-5.331-5.331s2.387-5.331 5.331-5.331c2.944 0 5.331 2.387 5.331 5.331s-2.387 5.331-5.331 5.331z"></path>
		         <path d="M26.462 7.456c0 1.060-0.859 1.919-1.919 1.919s-1.919-0.859-1.919-1.919c0-1.060 0.859-1.919 1.919-1.919s1.919 0.859 1.919 1.919z"></path>

		<script type="text/javascript">

            // Initialize Oxygen Modals
            jQuery(document).ready(function() {

                function showModal( modal ) {
                    var $modal = jQuery( modal );
                    $modal.addClass("live");
                    var modalId = $modal[0].querySelector('.ct-modal').id;
                    
                    var focusable = modal.querySelector('a[href]:not([disabled]), button:not([disabled]), textarea:not([disabled]), input[type="text"]:not([disabled]), input[type="radio"]:not([disabled]), input[type="checkbox"]:not([disabled]), select:not([disabled])');

                    if(focusable) {
                        setTimeout(() => {
                            focusable.focus();    
                        }, 500);
                    } else {
                        setTimeout(() => {
                        $modal.focus();
                        }, 500)
                    }

                    // Check if this modal can be shown according to settings and last shown time
                    // Current and last time in milliseconds
                    var currentTime = new Date().getTime();
                    var lastShownTime = localStorage && localStorage['oxy-' + modalId + '-last-shown-time'] ? JSON.parse( localStorage['oxy-' + modalId + '-last-shown-time'] ) : false;
                    // manual triggers aren't affected by last shown time
                    if( $modal.data( 'trigger' ) != 'user_clicks_element' ) {
                        switch( $modal.data( 'open-again' ) ) {
                            case 'never_show_again':
                                // if it was shown at least once, don't show it again
                                if( lastShownTime !== false ) return;
                                break;
                            case 'show_again_after':
                                var settingDays = parseInt( $modal.data( 'open-again-after-days' ) );
                                var actualDays = ( currentTime - lastShownTime ) / ( 60*60*24*1000 );
                                if( actualDays < settingDays ) return;
                                break;
                            default:
                                //always show
                                break;
                        }
                    }

                    // Body manipulation to prevent scrolling while modal is active, and maintain scroll position.
                    document.querySelector('body').style.top = `-${window.scrollY}px`;
                    document.querySelector('body').classList.add('oxy-modal-active');
                    
                    // save current time as last shown time
                    if( localStorage ) localStorage['oxy-' + modalId + '-last-shown-time'] = JSON.stringify( currentTime );

                    // trick to make jQuery fadeIn with flex
                    $modal.css("display", "flex");
                    $modal.hide();
                    // trick to force AOS trigger on elements inside the modal
                    $modal.find(".aos-animate").removeClass("aos-animate").addClass("aos-animate-disabled");

                    // show the modal
                    $modal.fadeIn(250, function(){
                        // trick to force AOS trigger on elements inside the modal
                        $modal.find(".aos-animate-disabled").removeClass("aos-animate-disabled").addClass("aos-animate");
                    });


                    if( $modal.data( 'close-automatically' ) == 'yes' ) {
                        var time = parseInt( $modal.data( 'close-after-time' ) );
                        if( $modal.data( 'close-after-time-unit' ) == 'seconds' ) {
                            time = parseInt( parseFloat( $modal.data( 'close-after-time' ) ) * 1000 );
                        }
                        setTimeout( function(){
                            hideModal(modal);
                        }, time );
                    }

                    // close modal automatically after form submit (Non-AJAX)
                    if( $modal.data( 'close-after-form-submit' ) == 'yes' && $modal.data("trigger") == "after_specified_time" ) {

                        // WPForms
                        // WPForms replaces the form with a confirmation message on page refresh
                        if( $modal.find(".wpforms-confirmation-container-full").length > 0 ) {
                            setTimeout(function () {
                                hideModal(modal);
                            }, 3000);
                        }

                        // Formidable Forms
                        // Formidable Forms replaces the form with a confirmation message on page refresh
                        if( $modal.find(".frm_message").length > 0 ) {
                            setTimeout(function () {
                                hideModal(modal);
                            }, 3000);
                        }

                        // Caldera Forms
                        // Caldera Forms replaces the form with a confirmation message on page refresh
                        if( $modal.find(".caldera-grid .alert-success").length > 0 ) {
                            setTimeout(function () {
                                hideModal(modal);
                            }, 3000);
                        }

                    }
                }

                window.oxyShowModal = showModal;

                var hideModal = function ( modal ) {

                    // Body manipulation for scroll prevention and maintaining scroll position
                    var scrollY = document.querySelector('body').style.top;
                    document.querySelector('body').classList.remove('oxy-modal-active');
                    document.querySelector('body').style.top = '';
                    window.scrollTo(0, parseInt(scrollY || '0') * -1);

                    // The function may be called by third party code, without argument, so we must close the first visible modal
                    if( typeof modal === 'undefined' ) {
                        var openModals = jQuery(".oxy-modal-backdrop.live");
                        if( openModals.length == 0 ) return;
                        modal = openModals[0];
                    }

                    var $modal = jQuery( modal );
                    // refresh any iframe so media embedded this way is stopped
                    $modal.find( 'iframe').each(function(index){
                        this.src = this.src;
                    });
                    // HTML5 videos can be stopped easily
                    $modal.find( 'video' ).each(function(index){
                        this.pause();
                    });
                    // If there are any forms in the modal, reset them
                    $modal.find("form").each(function(index){
                        this.reset();
                    });

                    $modal.find(".aos-animate").removeClass("aos-animate").addClass("aos-animate-disabled");

                    $modal.fadeOut(400, function(){
                        $modal.removeClass("live");
                        $modal.find(".aos-animate-disabled").removeClass("aos-animate-disabled").addClass("aos-animate");
                    });
                };

                window.oxyCloseModal = hideModal;

                jQuery( ".oxy-modal-backdrop" ).each(function( index ) {

                    var modal = this;

                    (function( modal ){
                        var $modal = jQuery( modal );
						
						var exitIntentFunction = function( e ){
                            if( e.target.tagName == 'SELECT' ) { return; }
							if( e.clientY <= 0 ) {
								showModal( modal );
								document.removeEventListener( "mouseleave", exitIntentFunction );
								document.removeEventListener( "mouseout", exitIntentFunction );
							}
						}

                        switch ( jQuery( modal ).data("trigger") ) {

                            case "on_exit_intent":
                                document.addEventListener( "mouseleave", exitIntentFunction, false);
								document.addEventListener( "mouseout", exitIntentFunction, false);
                                break;

                            case "user_clicks_element":
                                jQuery( jQuery( modal ).data( 'trigger-selector' ) ).click( function( event ) {
                                    showModal( modal );
                                    event.preventDefault();
                                } );
                                break;

                            case "after_specified_time":
                                var time = parseInt( jQuery( modal ).data( 'trigger-time' ) );
                                if( jQuery( modal ).data( 'trigger-time-unit' ) == 'seconds' ) {
                                    time = parseInt( parseFloat( jQuery( modal ).data( 'trigger-time' ) ) * 1000 );
                                }
                                setTimeout( function(){
                                    showModal( modal );
                                }, time );
                                break;

                            case "after_scrolled_amount":
                                window.addEventListener("scroll", function scrollDetection(){
                                    var winheight= window.innerHeight || (document.documentElement || document.body).clientHeight;
                                    var docheight = jQuery(document).height();
                                    var scrollTop = window.pageYOffset || (document.documentElement || document.body.parentNode || document.body).scrollTop;
                                    var isScrollUp = false;
                                    var oxyPreviousScrollTop = parseInt( jQuery( modal ).data( 'previous_scroll_top' ) );
                                    if( !isNaN( oxyPreviousScrollTop ) ) {
                                        if( oxyPreviousScrollTop > scrollTop) isScrollUp = true;
                                    }
                                    jQuery( modal ).data( 'previous_scroll_top', scrollTop );
                                    var trackLength = docheight - winheight;
                                    var pctScrolled = Math.floor(scrollTop/trackLength * 100);
                                    if( isNaN( pctScrolled ) ) pctScrolled = 0;

                                    if(
                                        ( isScrollUp && jQuery( modal ).data( 'trigger_scroll_direction' ) == 'up' ) ||
                                        ( !isScrollUp && jQuery( modal ).data( 'trigger_scroll_direction' ) == 'down' && pctScrolled >= parseInt( jQuery( modal ).data( 'trigger_scroll_amount' ) ) )
                                    ) {
                                        showModal( modal );
                                        window.removeEventListener( "scroll", scrollDetection );
                                    }
                                }, false);
                                break;
                            case "on_scroll_to_element":
                                window.addEventListener("scroll", function scrollDetection(){
                                    var $element = jQuery( jQuery( modal ).data( 'scroll_to_selector' ) );
                                    if( $element.length == 0 ) {
                                        window.removeEventListener( "scroll", scrollDetection );
                                        return;
                                    }

                                    var top_of_element = $element.offset().top;
                                    var bottom_of_element = $element.offset().top + $element.outerHeight();
                                    var bottom_of_screen = jQuery(window).scrollTop() + jQuery(window).innerHeight();
                                    var top_of_screen = jQuery(window).scrollTop();

                                    if ((bottom_of_screen > bottom_of_element - $element.outerHeight() /2 ) && (top_of_screen < top_of_element + $element.outerHeight() /2 )){
                                        showModal( modal );
                                        window.removeEventListener( "scroll", scrollDetection );
                                    }
                                }, false);
                                break;
                            case "after_number_of_clicks":
                                document.addEventListener("click", function clickDetection(){
                                    var number_of_clicks = parseInt( jQuery( modal ).data( 'number_of_clicks' ) );

                                    var clicks_performed = isNaN( parseInt( jQuery( modal ).data( 'clicks_performed' ) ) ) ? 1 :  parseInt( jQuery( modal ).data( 'clicks_performed' ) ) + 1;

                                    jQuery( modal ).data( 'clicks_performed', clicks_performed );

                                    if ( clicks_performed == number_of_clicks ){
                                        showModal( modal );
                                        document.removeEventListener( "click", clickDetection );
                                    }
                                }, false);
                                break;
                            case "after_time_inactive":
                                var time = parseInt( jQuery( modal ).data( 'time_inactive' ) );
                                if( jQuery( modal ).data( 'time-inactive-unit' ) == 'seconds' ) {
                                    time = parseInt( parseFloat( jQuery( modal ).data( 'time_inactive' ) ) * 1000 );
                                }
                                var activityDetected = function(){
                                    jQuery( modal ).data( 'millis_idle', 0 );
                                };
                                document.addEventListener( "click", activityDetected);
                                document.addEventListener( "mousemove", activityDetected);
                                document.addEventListener( "keypress", activityDetected);
                                document.addEventListener( "scroll", activityDetected);

                                var idleInterval = setInterval(function(){
                                    var millis_idle = isNaN( parseInt( jQuery( modal ).data( 'millis_idle' ) ) ) ? 100 :  parseInt( jQuery( modal ).data( 'millis_idle' ) ) + 100;
                                    jQuery( modal ).data( 'millis_idle', millis_idle );
                                    if( millis_idle > time ){
                                        clearInterval( idleInterval );
                                        document.removeEventListener( "click", activityDetected );
                                        document.removeEventListener( "mousemove", activityDetected );
                                        document.removeEventListener( "keypress", activityDetected );
                                        document.removeEventListener( "scroll", activityDetected );
                                        showModal( modal );
                                    }
                                }, 100);
                                break;

                            case "after_number_of_page_views":
                                var modalId = modal.querySelector('.ct-modal').id;
                                var pageViews = localStorage && localStorage['oxy-' + modalId + '-page-views'] ? parseInt( localStorage['oxy-' + modalId + '-page-views'] ) : 0;
                                pageViews++;
                                if( localStorage ) localStorage['oxy-' + modalId + '-page-views'] = pageViews;
                                if( parseInt( jQuery( modal ).data( 'number_of_page_views' ) ) == pageViews ) {
                                    if( localStorage ) localStorage['oxy-' + modalId + '-page-views'] = 0;
                                    showModal( modal );
                                }
                                break;

                        }

                        // add event handler to close modal automatically after AJAX form submit
                        if( $modal.data( 'close-after-form-submit' ) == 'yes' ) {

                            // Contact Form 7
                            if (typeof wpcf7 !== 'undefined') {
                                $modal.find('div.wpcf7').each(function () {
                                    var $form = jQuery(this).find('form');
                                    this.addEventListener('wpcf7submit', function (event) {
                                        if (event.detail.contactFormId == $form.attr("id")) {
                                            setTimeout(function () {
                                                hideModal(modal);
                                            }, 3000);
                                        }
                                    }, false);
                                });
                            }

                            // Caldera Forms
                            document.addEventListener( "cf.submission", function(event){
                                // Pending, Caldera AJAX form submissions aren't working since Oxygen 2.2, see: https://github.com/soflyy/oxygen/issues/1638
                            });

                            // Ninja Forms
                            jQuery(document).on("nfFormSubmitResponse", function(event, response){
                                // Only close the modal if the event was triggered from a Ninja Form inside the modal
                                if( $modal.find("#nf-form-" + response.id + "-cont").length > 0 ) {
                                    setTimeout(function () {
                                        hideModal(modal);
                                    }, 3000);
                                }
                            });

                        }

                    })( modal );

                });

                // handle clicks on modal backdrop and on .oxy-close-modal
                jQuery("body").on('click touchend', '.oxy-modal-backdrop, .oxy-close-modal', function( event ) {

                    var $this = jQuery( this );
                    var $target = jQuery( event.target );

                    // Click event in the modal div and it's children is propagated to the backdrop
                    if( !$target.hasClass( 'oxy-modal-backdrop' ) && !$this.hasClass( 'oxy-close-modal' ) ) {
                        //event.stopPropagation();
                        return;
                    }

                    if( $target.hasClass( 'oxy-modal-backdrop' ) && $this.hasClass( 'oxy-not-closable' ) ) {
                        return;
                    }

                    if( $this.hasClass( 'oxy-close-modal' ) ) event.preventDefault();

                    var $modal = $this.hasClass( 'oxy-close-modal' ) ? $this.closest('.oxy-modal-backdrop') : $this;
                    hideModal( $modal[0] );
                });

                jQuery(document).keyup( function(e){
                    if( e.key == 'Escape' ){
                        jQuery(".oxy-modal-backdrop:visible").each(function(index){
                            if( jQuery(this).data("close_on_esc") == 'on' ) hideModal(this);
                        });
                    }
                } );

            });

		</script>

<script type="text/javascript" id="ct_code_block_js_100133">var cursor = {
    delay: 8,
    _x: 0,
    _y: 0,
    endX: (window.innerWidth / 2),
    endY: (window.innerHeight / 2),
    cursorVisible: true,
    cursorEnlarged: false,
    $dot: document.querySelector('.cursor-dot'),
    $outline: document.querySelector('.cursor-dot-outline'),
    
    init: function() {
        // Set up element sizes
        this.dotSize = this.$dot.offsetWidth;
        this.outlineSize = this.$outline.offsetWidth;
        
        this.setupEventListeners();
        this.animateDotOutline();
    },
    
//     updateCursor: function(e) {
//         var self = this;
        
//         console.log(e)
        
//         // Show the cursor
//         self.cursorVisible = true;
//         self.toggleCursorVisibility();

//         // Position the dot
//         self.endX = e.pageX;
//         self.endY = e.pageY;
//         self.$dot.style.top = self.endY + 'px';
//         self.$dot.style.left = self.endX + 'px';
//     },
    
    setupEventListeners: function() {
        var self = this;
        
        // Anchor hovering
        document.querySelectorAll('a, #image-118-8, .button').forEach(function(el) {
            el.addEventListener('mouseover', function() {
                self.cursorEnlarged = true;
                self.toggleCursorSize();
            });
            el.addEventListener('mouseout', function() {
                self.cursorEnlarged = false;
                self.toggleCursorSize();
            });
        });
        
        // Click events
        document.addEventListener('mousedown', function() {
            self.cursorEnlarged = true;
            self.toggleCursorSize();
        });
        document.addEventListener('mouseup', function() {
            self.cursorEnlarged = false;
            self.toggleCursorSize();
        });
  
  
        document.addEventListener('mousemove', function(e) {
            // Show the cursor
            self.cursorVisible = true;
            self.toggleCursorVisibility();

            // Position the dot
            self.endX = e.pageX;
            self.endY = e.pageY;
            self.$dot.style.top = self.endY + 'px';
            self.$dot.style.left = self.endX + 'px';
        });
        
        // Hide/show cursor
        document.addEventListener('mouseenter', function(e) {
            self.cursorVisible = true;
            self.toggleCursorVisibility();
            self.$dot.style.opacity = 1;
            self.$outline.style.opacity = 1;
        });
        
        document.addEventListener('mouseleave', function(e) {
            self.cursorVisible = true;
            self.toggleCursorVisibility();
            self.$dot.style.opacity = 0;
            self.$outline.style.opacity = 0;
        });
    },
    
    animateDotOutline: function() {
        var self = this;
        
        self._x += (self.endX - self._x) / self.delay;
        self._y += (self.endY - self._y) / self.delay;
        self.$outline.style.top = self._y + 'px';
        self.$outline.style.left = self._x + 'px';
        
        requestAnimationFrame(this.animateDotOutline.bind(self));
    },
    
    toggleCursorSize: function() {
        var self = this;
        
        if (self.cursorEnlarged) {
            self.$dot.style.transform = 'translate(-50%, -50%) scale(0.75)';
            self.$outline.style.transform = 'translate(-50%, -50%) scale(1.5)';
        } else {
            self.$dot.style.transform = 'translate(-50%, -50%) scale(1)';
            self.$outline.style.transform = 'translate(-50%, -50%) scale(1)';
        }
    },
    
    toggleCursorVisibility: function() {
        var self = this;
        
        if (self.cursorVisible) {
            self.$dot.style.opacity = 1;
            self.$outline.style.opacity = 1;
        } else {
            self.$dot.style.opacity = 0;
            self.$outline.style.opacity = 0;
        }
    }
}

cursor.init();</script>
